invention ordained a very fair form and manner to plant there certain orders
of trees in proportion, amongst which there should be built fourteen ^^^le
Chappelles or stations, to represent the joys and sorrows of the holy mother
of God: and this to be contrived in such order and fashion that all the hill
should seem to appear in form of a ^^arre, which signifies the name of the
virgin Mary* And moreover it is to be provided of a hedge and ditch round about
that it may be Hortus conclusus, a Garden round (...): a name which the holy
scripture affords to our Lady. And besides all this our said Princes have made
there an oblation of a marvelous sumptuous ornament, together with a Chesuble
and Copes for the Deacon and Subdeacon to celebrate divine service therein.

THE XV. CHAPTER.
But to come to the miracles: let us begin with the entrance of the year 1603.
and some months before; after which time especially about Easter the principal
of them happened. And we will set them down according to every month, so far
forth as they came to our knowledge, adding unto the^ those which afterward
insued, as also those whereof we have gotten information (...) the first
publishing of this history: p^^cing every one in their due order, according to
the times in which they came to pas: to the end that our Lord (who vouchsafed
to work these things by the intercession of his Mother) might receive the
honor and glory which unto him is due, and that all Christians as well those
which are misguided and in error, as others might consider and touch with
their fingers, where the light of truth has her abode, and where is the true
sheep* fold, wherein they may expect and hope to obtain their everlasting
salvation.

Of a blind wooman which was cured.
PEtronel Riders wife to Lambert Bauduin About the month of May or June 160^.
sometime soldier, and launcier under the Lord of Grobbendonck in the Country
of Brabant, in the year 1602. being at Dust had a great defluction of humors,
which fell upon her eyes, and a great and vehement grief insued thereupo^ as if
her eyes had been gnawne with some vermin: which increaced so much that she
utterly lost her sight: notwithstanding that many medicines were applied unto
her both by the advice of surgeons, as others, of which she received no help at
all: in such sort that she could not see or decerne any thing in the world
which continued more then eight or ten days. At which time a certain woman
seeing her in this plight, advised her to go unto our Lady at Montaigu where
many had been cured of their agues, hoping that there she should find some help
for her disease. Moreover she counseled her to wash her eyes with the water
which is behynd the Chapel of the foresaid Montaigu. Whereupon the said
Petronel resolved to go thither in pilgrimage, and having sought out a woman
in Die to lead her, she walked (starck blind) toward the said Montaigu
about the Month of May or, June, in the said year 1602: but as soon as she
began to go up the hill toward the chapel, she felt the accustomed griefs of
her eyes to be much assuaged, and with all her self to be much inwardly
comforted. Which alteration after she had perceived, she would needs try
whether she had recovered any thing of her sight or no, so that with her
fingers lifting up her eyelids, she perceived that she began to see (as it
were through an obscure mist) the grass and bushes of the Mountain, and a
little afterward setting somewhat forwards, she perfectly saw the little
chapel of wood where the Image of our Lady was placed, and hereupon* she
spoke to the woman which led her, and thancking her for her pains told her
that she needed her help no longer, for that she had now recovered her
sight: and so the said Petronel went alone without any other aid toward the
foresaid water, where having washed her eyes, she fell to her devotions in the
Chapel of our Lady, rendering thancks to God and her, for this worck of
mercy: and so returning whole and merry to her hows at Die has ever since
inioyed perfectly her sight, and has been free from al her former pains, and
yet so remains to this present day, as it appeared upon the six and twentieth
of June in the year 1604. when in the city of Bruxelles before the
Magistrates there by solemn oath she affirmed all that has been said,
conformable to an act framed thereof subsigned P. Numan Secretaire, and sealed
with the s^ale of the said City.

How blood was found, upon the lips of the Image of our Lady.
Upon the third of January in the year 1603. diverse Magistrates and The third
of January 1603.
other persons were met together at Sichen from the next villages about some
affairs appertayning to that quarter. Amongst others Matthew O^de^^^gge
Escheuin of Bekeu^rt, Walter V^kelen Escheuin of VVanr^de, Henry Reymakers
Escheuin of VVersbeke, Bartholmew Schellens, and Laurens of Ca^ten were there
preset. Who after they had ended all their business at Sichen, returning
homeward, and passing by Montaigu, they did their devotions in the Chapel of
our Lady; and whilst they were in prayer, the said Walter Vnkelen espied a
drop of blood upon the lip of the image of our Lady, whereupon drawing near
to the image, he wyped of the drop with his finger, and he found that it was
perfect blood, and incontinently an other like drop returned, the which was
wyped away by Matthew O^de^^ogge: and as an other the third time appeared, it
was wyped of by Henry Reymakers: and the foresaid Walter Vnk^len seeing the
fourth drop of blood to appear upon the lip, took a cloth or handkerchief,
and dried it, and found a marck of very blood in the same, even such as might
issue out of the body of a living man: whereupon they were meruelously
astonished: and the next morning this Walter looking upon his hand-kerchief,
found the said drop to have spread itself as large as an English groate, and
some what bleaker of color then it was the day before. These aforenamed
persons while yet they were in the Chapel, looked diligently on every side,
to see whether the Image might receive any moisture through the roof, but they
found no sign at all of any such thing: for it was a very fair and clear
Sunne-shyny day, and there was never any paynting or color laid on the picture
so far as any man could remember. And all this which has been said, was
auerred by the foresaid persons, under their sole^n oaths before the
Magistrates of the town of S^^hen, in the presence of many witnesses, as
appears by a writing made hereof, and subsigned L. van Ogernen, and sealed
with the seal of the said town: and it is very certain, that in the first
three months of this accident, to wit, in the holy week before Easter, the
said picture by reason of the oldnes thereof, by the appointment of the Curate
and Church-warde^s was newly painted.

How a lame maid was healed.
MArie Lenkens daughter of Francis In April. ^. ^3.
Lenkens and Cat^arin Vermo^en being ten years of age, had an accident that
happened her in her right leg, in the year 1599, in such sort that the said leg
was shrunck up and became three fingers shorter then the other, and withal
smaller and slenderer, in which sort she continued for three years space
together, although with great anguish and pain, and the third year she was
not able to go therewith in any sort, whereupon her mother resolved toe go
with her in pilgrimage to our lady of Montaigu: the which she did upon the
feast of the Annunciation of the virgin Marie, in the said year 1603, putting
her daughter on horsback, and being come to the river of Demere, near to a
place called Tystelt, where by horse they were notable to pass they sent the
said horse back again, and they both walked together on foot toward Montaigu,
the poor lame maiden halting downright, and often falling to the ground,
before they could arrive at the Chapel of our Lady: Where being come
exceedingly weerie, they did their devotions: which being ended, the maid
recovered so much strength, that she returned home with her mother on foot,
without any molestation pain or wearines neither at that present time, or ever
after: and since that time her leg by little and little grew of aequall bigness
and length with the other, in such sort that she now walks without any
difficulty, wheresoever she pleases, as well as any other. Al which has been
affirmed by her mother under her solemn oath before the Magistrates of the town
of Ar^t^^t: and Marie vander N^is widow of Christian vanden Vinne dwelling in
Arschot, who accompanied them in their pilgrimage, together with Henry Godfrey
Michtels, who was neighbor unto the said maid, did in lyk sort under their
oaths avouch before the said Magistrates, that they had seen and known the
foresaid maid lame and impotent, and afterward to have been miraculously
cured, as has been said: all which appears by an act made thereof by the said
Magistrates, bearing date the xxixth of March in the year 1604, subsigned P.
Aelbrechts, and sealed with the seal of the town of Arschos.

How a man sick of the palsy was healed.
PEser of Honsberg Escheuin of Merhout In April, 1601.
in the Campignie, being of the age of one and fifty years, fell suddenly
into a great disease, in the end of the Month of January 1606, the which
continuing for ten or twelve days space, thereupon ensued so great a palsy,
that he was deprived of the use of his arms and legs, and of all his other
members, his head eyes and tongue only excepted, which he was able to move.
And besides this, he had a grief that was so vehement and continual, that he
could neither sleep or rest day or night: in such sort that from Palmesunday
till eight days after Easter he was fame to have every night at least two,
sometimes three or four of his family to watch with him, and to administer
unto him his necessities, sometimes to carry him to the fire, and presently
back to his bed again. Who albeit he had used the counsel and receiptes of some
Physicians for his recure, yet felt he no ease at all, but rather increase of
his grief which made him wholly to give them over. And whereas certain of the
inhabitants of Merbou^ had related unto him that by the invocation of Gods
Mother many miracles were wrought at Mo^taig^^ near to Die, he entering into a
fervent and zealous resolution, to take her for his refuge, and to go in
pilgrimage to that place: and withal to Boxtele in the Campigni^, where the
miraculous blood of the holy Sacrament of the altar is reserved; in the mean
while with many tears and groans calling upon the glorious virgin Mary, and
with great desire expecting the feast of the Annunciation of our Lady, (which
was very near, and was that year translated til after the octaues of Easter,
for that it fell in the holy week;) and so much the more because he had
understood that diverse of his neighbors were resolved that day to go in
pilgrimage to Montaig^, which day of the Annunciatio^ when it came, he caused
himself to be carried in a wagon to the foresaid mountain, continually
afflicted with the palsy and impote^cie of all his limbs: save only that
some two or three days before his departure, and whylst his servants made
ready those things which were necessary for his voyage, he began a little to
move his fingers. Being therefore the same day arrived at Montaigu, he found
such a throng of people, that he could not in any wise come near unto the
Chapel. For which cause, to satisfy his devotion, they brought him the image
of our lady to the waggo where he lay, the which with much reverence he
kissed: and after the press of the people was past, his wife withone of his
servants and two others carried him three times about the said Chapel: and no
sooner was he put again into the wagon, but he felt in himself a great change
and ease: in such sort that he thought himself wholly cured: but trying to move
himself, he found that he was as yet impotent and without the use of his
limbs. Notwithstanding being returned home, he felt that his palsy by little
and little from that day forward began to decreace: and every day after he
found himself better, in so much that in short time he recovered so great force
and health, that he could permit himself to be led through his hows: and a
little while after he walked without any help of his crutches, which also with
in few days he laid aside, walking only with a staf in his hand, and not long
after without either staf or any other help at all: in such sort that this
Ho^sberge being restored to perfect health and strength, and use of his limbs,
failed not to render thancks to God, and his holy Mother: and upon the eigth of
the month of September next following being the day of the Nativity of the
glorious Virgin, he departed from his hows on horseback, to offer unto our Lady
one of his Crutches wherewith he was wont to support himself: and from the town
of Sichen he went on foot to the Chapel of Mo^taig^, where he did his
devotion, and gave God thancks for the mercy which he received as has been
said. And since that time he has continued well disposed and healthie, as he is
at this present And this that has been here said, is set down in the Register
of the said Chap pel upon the eigth day of Septembre 1603. And as by the said
Honsberg it was again declared (being su^moned thereunto) under his solemn
oath before the court and Magistrates of Merbo^t, upon the seventh of March in
the year 1604. Upon which day VVillebrord Bosmans, Adrian Verhelle^ and John
S^i^ne^ Escheuines of the same place, declared and avouched, that they had
diverse times see^ and visited this Honsberg while he was sick, and that they
found him altogether taken with the palsy and impotent and deprived of the use
of his limbs. Al which is conformable to that which the magistrate has set
down, dated as before, and subsigned John Trudo^ius Secretary: and sealed with
their seal.

A cure of one that was blind and taken with the Apoplexy.
ANne Vereyken the wife of Hubert VVell^^s dwelling in the village of In May
1603.
Test^l^, not far from the town of Sichen was in the month of February in
the year 1603. taken with the Apoplexy, and there with also lost her sight in
so much that her husband was forced to carry or lead her to every place,
whether she would go. And although many medicines were applied to cure her
disease, yet she found no help or cure at all: wherefore she took her refuge
toward our Lady, and made a promis to go and visit her at Montaigu, the
which when she had accomplished in the month of May next following, she
recovered her sight and the intier health of al her body, and went up and down
wheresoever it pleased her, and always afterward remained in good state as she
is at this present. All this here related, was according to order of law
declared both by her self and her husband before the Magistrates of Siche^, as
well upon the eleventh of May in the foresaid year 1603, ^s also upon the one
and twentieth of April 1604. According to a writing framed hereof and signed
L^van Ogernen Secretary, and sealed with the town seal.

The punishment of one that scoffed at the Pilgrimage of Mountaigu.
A Certain townesman of Die (whose name for certain causes we do not In May
1603.
set down) began to mock at such as went in Pilgrimage to Montaigu, and a
little after was stricke^ in his body, in such sort that he became lame, and
altogether deprived of the use of his limbs, and sustai ned such vehement
torments that he was constrained to keep his bed: and although he had procured
certain medicines and remedies to be ministered unto him, yet could he not be
helped. Wherefore at last resolving with himself to go and visit our Lady at
Montaigu: and having obtained some strength after this his resolution, he
walked thither by little and little on foot: and so soon as he had performed
his pilgrimage, he recovered and was wholly cured, as it appears by the
information hereof taken in the town of Die, by certain commissioners that
were sent thither by the Right Reverend the Lord Archbishop of Maclin.

How a Child that was in a consumption and blind was healed.
I Oane Ma^s the widow of Lewis Castel^ In May 160^.
dwelling in the town of Die, had a child of one year old or thereabout: who
was taken with a great malady, which kept him in his bed more the^ three whole
months continually, whereby he was brought so low, that he had nothing left but
skin and bones: he had moreover a swelling in his throat, which by diverse
surgeons was judged to be some vain that was broken, by others, that it was
some evil matter or humor which was descended thither. And besides these he
had an accident in his eye, the which being showed to the surgeons, they were
of opinion that the eye was broken out, and that the piece of the sight was
corrupted, as in very deed the child could see nothing therewith* and they were
persuaded that he should never see with it so long as he lived: the which child
was come to those terms, that his mother expected no other thing of him but
that he should shortly die. Nowithstanding putting her confidence in the mercy
of God, and in the assistance of his most sacred Mother, she resolved to go
with her Child, and to visit our Lady at Mo^taigu on three several Frydayes:
and notwithstanding that the mother was also ^^^k, yet she accomplished her
Pilgrimage in the beginning of the so^mer, in the year 1603. And the first day
that she was at the Chapel, she laid her child upon the altar, so long as she
made her prayer: which being ended, and returning homeward, the child fell
sweetly a sleep in her arms, and so continued til she came to Die: and in
this so^te persisting in her devotions the two next frydayes following, the
child was made whole and sound, and by little and little recovered the perfect
health both of his body and of his eye; with which he now ^^eth very clearly,
and remains in very good plight. All this those of the Court of Die have
witnessed, after the hearing and examination of the a foresaid Ioane,
conformable to a writing that was drawn thereof, bearing date the XXth of March
1604. subsigned I. vanden Goedenhu^se, and sealed with the seal of the said
town,

One cured of the Iaunders and Squinancie.
THe Lady Francis de i^^ombeck, Abbess In May 1603.
of the Cloister of Hoght near to the city of Maestright in the Duchy of
Braba^t in the beginning of May, 1603, was attain ted with the Iaunders,
whereof she became so sick, that having had the advice of a certain Phisitio^
which dwelled at Lie ge he was in despair of her life as he plain ly affirmed
to Dame Catharin Cortilz, Religiouse of the said Convent, yet he sent the said
lady Abbess some herbs with a certain drink, but it profited her nothing and
as her disease daily increased, so that she had little hope by any way of
Physic, she committed her self unto God almighty, and to the help of the
glorious Virgin Marie, promising by vow unto God and her, a pi^grim^g^ and an
alms unto the chapel of our Lady at Montaigu, and two or three days after
she s^nt thither he^ maid O^ae T(...)r ma^^, the which was con upon the xxv^i*
rof May in the foresaid year 1603. who having ended her devotion she brought
her Lady a piece of the Oak wherein the blessed Virgins Image was set: the
which the said lady Abbess receiving with all reverence and devotion, caused
it to be applied to every thing that either she did eat or drinck: trusting in
God, and hoping through the intercession of his holy mother that she should
find remedy thereby, and from that day she began oame^d and to recover
perfectly her health, without any human help: in so much that a little while
after she was made whole and sound. Afterward the^e happened unto her a great
sorenes and pain in her throat, which Physitio^s call the Squinancie, whereby
she was brought again into manifest peril of death, as the surgeon openly
declared whom they had sent for to help her. Her tongue and throat were so
inflamed, that they seemed altogether black: and although, they opened a vain
in her tongue, three or fowr times together, yet it helped nothing, for not one
drop of blood would come forth, which when the-sayd Lady Abbess had
perceived, and understanding the danger wherein she was, she vowed an other
pilgrimage to our Lady of Montaigu, and sent thither again the foresaid Oda,
and VVindel Corenborst her servants, who having ended their devotions upon the
xxvj. of June 1603. the-sayd Lady Abbess recovered afterward, and within
few days returned to her perfect health. As it well appears by her
attestatio^ signed with her own hand, and sealed with her seal.

Of a lame and impotent man healed.
BE^^ra^d de Loyarbre locksmith dwelling at H^y in the cuntrie of Liege, was,
(some three years past) attached with a In May 2603.
vehement pain in his reins, and about his heart, in such sort that he could
not follow his occupatio^ except very seldom and that fair and softly: the
which pain continued very long, and at one time for the space of six whole
months: whereby he was brought so low, that he was constrained to keep his
bed, from October 1602, until Easter eve 1603. and then (although he was very
sick) he endeavored to rise, but he found his left beg (by the long and
continual pains thereof) to be much shrunck up, and by a good foot to have
become shorter then the other, whereby he was forced to take two crutches, and
with them he walked in great pain and feeblenes. So it came to pass, that on
the day of S. Peter and S. Paul, being the xxix. of ^^^e, in the foresaid
year 1603. he hard some relate the miracles of our Lady of Montaigu: whereby
he was so moved, that he purposed with a great and fervent desire to go thither
on foot with his crutches, and alone with out the assistance of any other:
which he did, walking on very slowly, although not without great grief and
labor of his body: in such sort, that within fowr days and an half he came
to the Chapel at Mo^taigu, which for all this was not past ten miles distant
from H^y: having his hands and fingers much swollen, and the skin worn of by
the continual handling of his crutches, with had also much opened or strained
his arm pittes. And being now come before the Chapel, he made there
devoutly his prayers unto God and his glorious Mother, which being e^^s^d, he
raised up himself fair and softly without his crutches, and began to walk
praying about the Chapel, although not without great pain: but at the second
time he felt a certain soudaine puff of vvynd, to come down as it were from
heaven upon him, in so much as he feared he should have been thrown down to
the earth, by which vvynd he felt a kind of motion and svveet heat to enter
in to his body, whereby he thought his interior parts were vvarmed and
wholy altered: and so going the third time about, he found himself intierly
cured; and that his left leg (which before was a foot shorter then the right)
was now made longer and aeq^ual with the other, and that he could well use
it: yea, he found it stonger then his leg that before was whole: where with
being much comforted, having re^dred tha^ckes to God, and his holy Mother, who
had prayed for him, he left there his crutches, and walked homeward to Huy on
foot without them. And in August next following, and an other time after that,
he came on foot to Montaign, in memory and gratitude of the favor he had
there received: and the^ he was much eased of the pain he felt about his heart,
which he had very long endured. All this which here has bee^ set down, this
Bertra^d declared at Mo^taigu, before M. James de Castro, doctor of divinity
and Deane of the Christiantie of Die, Sir Godfrey Thie^ win^kle Curate of
Sichen, Master Ioachim de Buschere Secretary of the Cou^cil of Brabant, Peter
de Hem Notarie, and many others who were then present: and after this again it
was all affirmed and verified under a solemn oath by the foresaid Bertrand
(being summoned thereunto) before the sworn Bourgemaister* and Council of the
said town of Huy, as it appears by their attestation made under their seal,
and signed by the secretary of the same town, dated the xvijth. of January
1604.

Of one that had a withred hand, and how it was afterward healed.
MArie Isertant the daughter of Andrew Isertant, dwelling at Esselbeke near In
I^ne 160^.
to ^ousso^, hand by the City of Aken, was in the year 1603. surprised with a
great mailadie, whereof she feeling her self abettred, endeavored to go into a
cave of the hows to fetch something thence, and being come to the last step,
was suddenly taken with a certain kind of Appoplexie: which made her fall
down to the grownd, having much hurt her self on her left side, and especially
her hand and foot on that side, in such sort that she could do no manner of
woork: and was forced to walk with a crutch, for other wise she was not able to
go and in this manner she continued ten whole weeks.

In the mean while, having hard report of the miracles which by the
invocation of our Lady, were wrought at Mo^taigue she resolved likewise to go
thither for the recovery of her health: and arrived at the place upon the xxth
of June, in the same year 1603. and so soon as she drew near to the mountain,
she began to feel a great, yea an intolerable gnawing, in her left hand, which
was so lame, fast closed together, and dead, that she had no feeling thereof,
no not when they pricked it with any sharp pointed thing. When with certain of
her neighbors she was come up to the Chapel, they went about it some times on
foot, some times on their knees, making their prayers very devoutly: and forth
with her dry and dead hand opened of it self, to the great admiration and
comfort both of her self, and of all those that assisted her. For more proof
whereof, withdrawing her self into a cottage which was in that mountain, made
her self ready and dressed her head, as well with the one hand as with the other,
and this in the sight of very many: which for the space of the foresaid te^
weeks she was never able to do: and thus returning whole to her home, she
continued ever after very well, as she remains at this present xth of March in
the year 1604. On which day she affirmed and avouched all that has been said,
in the foresaid city of Aken in the presence of Master Peeter Hensenius
Lice^tiate in divinity, Curate of S. Foillie^, S^eue^ Radermaker de Kelmis
maier of E^eburg near unto Esselbeke, Leonard Loop de Kelmis and Brice Isertant
brother unto this Marie, all which last three did in like manner affirm, that
they had see^ the said Marie attainted with the Apoplexy and palsy, as has
been said, conformable to a writing framed here of bearing the date above
specified.

Of a lame young man cured.
HEnry Capenbergh son of John Capenbergh In July 1603.
dwelling near unto Kerckraid, in the territory of Shertogen-rode in the
Cuntrie beyond the Me^se, was lame of both his legs, and so had continued
eight years continualy, in such sort, that he could hardly go with crutches:
and although his father had caused all ma^n ^ of remedies and medecines to be
applied unto him, yet could he not procure him any help or ease at all. But
after he had hard tell of the miracles which were wrought at Montaigu, he took
his way thitherward with his crutches, to perform there his devotion, hoping,
that the glorious Mother of God would not fail to assist him, and to pray for
him. At which place he arrived the second of Iulie 1603. being the feast of
the Visitatio^ of our Lady, and there offered up his prayers right devoutly
before the Chapel: which being ended, he felt himself much eased and in
better order the^ before: and as he returned homeward, passing by Ake^ and
there praying to the Virgin Marie in her church which is in that city, he
found himself so much bettered, that there he left and offered up one of his
crutches. Neuer-the-lesse once again he returned with one crutche to Montaigu,
in the end of the aforesaid month, where having renewed his prayers, he found
himself perfectly whole and recovered, so that leaving his other crutch at our
Ladies Chapel, home he returned safe and sound, with out the help of any to
assist him, as he still continues, and was so upon the xviijth. of February in
the year 1604, on which day he declared and affirmed the foresaid
particularities, before the Magistrates of Ache as is to be seen by a writing
penned thereof, subsigned Nicolaus Munsterus Secretary, and sealed with the
seal of thesayd City.

Of a woman that was cured of many strange accidents.
IOane Cas, wife unto William de Bois In July 1603.
dwelling at Ia^bez in the suburbs of the City of Namures* was broken on both
^^des, each rupture coming forth as bigg as ones fist: the which she had
endured for the space of eleue^ or twelve years. And in the year 1601. in the
month of May throwing hay out of her loft, down she fell, and broke her right
leg, to the cure whereof she e^ploied many remedies and medcines, but she

in such sort that she was constained to walk with a crutch, and her leg
remained very full of pain. Moreover in the year 1603, in the month of Iulie,
her stomach swelled as great as a man's head, whether it was by any inward
rupture of that part which Physicians call P^ritonau^, in which the bowels are
contained, or by some other accident, so it was, that it bred in her such a
disease and vexation, that she was brought to such extremity, that she was
reddy to give up the ghost, and this according to the judgment of her Curate,
and of Master Hermes Petit Doctor of Physic in Namures. The patie^t being in
these terms, it happened that a certain woman of her acquaintance called
Catharin Meurisse came to visit her, who seeing her in such anxietie and
danger, counseled her, and said, she might do well to vow some Pilgrimage to our
Lady at Montaigu near to Sichen, affirming that she her self by this means
was cured of the grauel wherewith she had been long time afflicted. Which when
the said patient had hard, whith great devotion she said, that she did promise
to go that Pilgrimage through the grace and assistance of almighty God. And on
the same day about some three hours after she had thus promised, the aforesaid
Ioane Cas found her self intierly whole and cured, as well of her Rupt^^es, as of
the swelling of her stomach: and so rising out of her bed, she began to walk up
and down her hows, not only without her cruch wherewith she was wount to help
herself before, but also without any stick or staff or any other thing else to
support her. And from that day forward she could go with one shoe vnderlayd
and made higher the breadth of ones hand, because her broken leg was become so
much more short the^ the other. And in October following, she accomplished her
pilgrimage to our Lady at Montaigu as before she had vowed; which when she had
performed, she felt greater ease in her leg the^ before, in so much that her
shoe is now but of an inch high, which was of a handbredth high before. And
all this that has been here set down, the said Joan Cas declared and verified
under her solemn o^he, in the hands of C. R^m^s Notarie, in presence of the
Reverend Sir Giles Bosman Chanon and Archpriest of the Bishopric of Namures,
and Pierchon Pimperneau witnesses, comfortable to a public writing framed
hereof, and subsigned by the said Notarie and dated the ixth. of April 1604.

How a wenche was suddenly healed of many soars.
WAlter Gilton glasier and Marie de In Aug. 1^03.
Rau^schot his wife, burge^^s and inhabitants of the City of Louaine had
amongst other children a daughter of thirteen years of age, called Catharin,
which child in the year 1600. fell into an infirmity and disease which is
commonly called the kings evil, or the evil of S. Marcoul, Because that saint
in France does he^^e this disease in such as at his tomb comme^d them selves
to his holy intercessi^
which broke out into more then an hundred holes, running with matter down all
her body, hands, arms, neck, face, eyes, belly, legs and feet, before and
behynd and on every ^yd: and her mouth was swollen as big as three mouths,
and in like manner was her nose and all her face, and her eyes were so swollen
and full of pain, that she was scarce able to see: and she became so weak that
she could not live, and yet she could not die: being sometimes in such pitiful
sort afflicted, that for the space of three months she could not stir out of
her bed, neither could she move either hand or foot: and further more when so
ever she rose up out of her bed, she could not go one step without the help of
a staff. To remedy which disease, her parents used the advice and Counsel of
many Doctors of Physic, and Surgeons, who had prescribed her many drincks and
drugges, but ^ll was to no purpose or prosit at all. Afterward an other very
skilful and famous Surgeon dwelling in that City of L^^^i^^ called M. Rombold
walters, being much commended unto the^, they couenaunted with him for a
certain so^me of money, that he would take in hand to cure their daughter,
wherein he took great pains, visiting and employing his labor and skill about
her, twyse every day, for six months space, and yet for all this could he not
obtain his desired purpos. These things having thus continued for the space of
three years, and this poor* Catharin having hard report of the miracles of
our Lady at Montaigu, and amongst others how a certain lame woman was there
cured: she importuned her parents, that they would vouchesafe to go with her
unto that place of pilgrimage: to which her request they yielded, and promised
they would so do: and where as her father intended to carry her on his back the
child would not permit that, but rather resolved to go thither her self on
soot, saying that she would force her self thereunto: and she hoped that she
should perform that voyage on foot, and so upon the second of August 1603.
they made the^ selves reddie for their journey, and they put on their daughter
a clean smock, taking from her that which she had worn, the which (be it
written with reverence to the reader) was stif with the filth and matter* which
did yslue out of the soars of her body: and putting a staff in her hand,
after they had dyned they deparfrom L^^ame, having in their company ^^^^^
C^^ema^s and his wife, Martin L^^^^^^ and others of their neighbors: and that
night they went and lodged at a village called T^ielt, with is distant some
three miles from the foresaid City, having much stayed by the way, by reason
of the great difficulty the said wench had to go. The next day in the morning
notwithstanding that it rained (which was very troublesome to the patient)
they took their way forwards toward Montaigu, where they arrived before
midday, and there did their devotion at the Chapel of our Lady, from the time
of their arriual til after dinner, and there offered up a child made in wax:
and having continued their prayers for one hours space, they retired
themselves into a booth or cottage hard by, and there reposed themselves,
expecting til the rain (which still continued) would cease: but when they saw
it ceased not, they all set forwards on foot with the little maid, to return
home again. In which their return the patie^t (although she had alredie gone
so much that day) walked with better courage, then she had done before, whereat
all those of her company were much astonished, and the said patient passed on
her way singing sometimes certain sonnets which the children of her years are
wount ordinarily to sing. And being now come within half a mile of L^uai^e the
Father seeing his daughter to wax somewhat werie, he carried her on his back
until he came to the city gates: and so soon as they were at home, the mother
put the child into her bed as she was accustomed to do: and she passed that
night very quietly, but the next morning the maid arose and put on her apparel
without any help, and came down, and told her mother that she had no filth or
matter on her smock, and that she felt no grief at all in her body, but that
she found her self wholly cured. Whereupon her Father and Mother searched her
with all diligence, and found her smock fair and clean, without any spotts at
all, and which was more, they found al her sores, which were very many to be
wholly cured and shut up, and especially on her belly (where her grief was
greatest before) and that all was strong and quite gone: yea leaving very few
scares behynd: in such sort that her mother finding her thus cured made no
difficulte to let her ly that very night following with the rest of her
Children who were well in health: the which for three yeare^ before she durst
never have permitted. After this she remained whole and well, not troubled with
any grief in the world and so she continues even to this present day. And
since her cure she has been twice at Montaigue, once on foot, and another time
by wagon, to render thancks to God and his glorious Mother for so great and
singular a benefit. All this that has been said, was affirmed and auerred by
both the parents of the child, before the Magistrates of the said city of
Lo^ain, upon the xxvjth. of June in the year 1604, and upon the self same day
the above named next neighbors of the foresaid walter Gilton, made their
appare^ce before the said Magistrates, who did in semblable manner affirm and
declare, that they had sundry times seen the foresaid wench, both before and
after her Pilgrimage to Montaigu: and that before she was in the a foresaid
evil case, and that afterward she miraculously and perfectly was cured, as
has been said. As it appears by the attestation of the aforesaid Magistrates
and dated as above, subsigned R. le Prince, and sealed with the seal of the
same city.

How a man whose legs were eaten with the canker was healed.
HEnry Loye^ alias de Visschere being of In Aug. 1603.
75 years of age, dwelling in the Village of Rerthem, near to the City of
Lo^ain had about midsomer 1603. his legs and feet so grievously swollen, that he
could put on no shoes, the pain was so excessive which he endured: and in the
month of Iulte in the same year there burst out in each of his legs a hole
near to the ancle and instep of the foot: the which holes within eight days
grew so bad, and became so large and deep, that on the one side a man might put
in his three fingers, and on the other side there was dead flesh of the length
of ones finger: and the patient affirmed that he felt such pain thereof, as if
it had bin g^awn by dogs. The which some judged to be the ca^ker, for that
the edges of the wounds were full of dead black flesh: and that from the bottom
the blood always issued out with so terrible a stentche, that no creature was
able to endure it: and as they perceived that the poor patient found no help by
any thing that he applied, he was counseled by some person, to go and visit our
Lady at Montaigu: which he promised and vowed to do, in hope there to receive
some consolation, and he never left to proceed in his intent, until he was
carried thither: but for so much a^ he was so sick and weak, none durst take the
matter upon them, except he were first put in the state of grace, for fear
least he should have dyed in the way as he went. The which thing after the
patient had understood, he caused himself to be carried to the Church of
B^rthem, where he made his confession, and communicated, the blood running from
him by the way as he went. And a few days after, to wit upon the fifth of
August in the aforesaid year 1603. he made himself to be carried in a wagon
unto Montaigu, where at our Ladies Chapel he did his devotion: and a certain
Priest that then was there, cou^seled him that he should make twice more that
voyage, and that for this purpose he should make choice of the Friday, and that
he should have a good confidence in the assistance of the Mother of God. The
patie^t being returned home he found his legs much lesser and vnswolne, and
the pain thereof much more tolerable then before. Whereupon following the
Counsel that was given him, he returned again the second time by waggo^ to
Montaigu, upon the feast of the Assumption of our Lady: and after he had ended
his prayers, he found much more ease then before. And upon the next friday,
being the xxij of the same month, he was brought thither the third time, and
did his devotions as before, and having at every of these times been led thrice
about the Chapel, not without effusion of his blood, which ran from his
legs upon the earth, together with a very great stenche as diverse of Montaigu
reported, who then were present. And from thence being come home, he fell into
so great weakness and such a swouning that every one thought he should have
forth with given up his ghost: the which being over passed he affirmed that
he felt a great and notable amendment of his legs and after that day the two
great wounds in his legs were by little and little cured and filled up of
themselves, and all the dead and corrupt flesh became good. So as the same
patient remains cured even at this present, having nothing le^t him but the
scarres of the soars, which are each of the^ of a span in greatness. All which
is well known by an authentical attestatio^ made before the Curate, Maier and
Escheuins, of the said village of Berche^, upon the xxij. of February 1604.
and sealed with the ordinary seal of that village.

The healing of a bunche.
SIster B^trice Ieroo^s a lay sister professed In Aug. 1603.
in the Cloister of S. Vrsula or of the eleven thousand Virgins, in a place
called the Halfstreet in the City of Louain^ In this monaste rye a ver ^^ous
and venerable co^^^^nie of English gen^^evvomen ^^e profested.
contracted upon the year^ 160^. a certain accident, betwixt the right pap and
her shoulder before, which was a kind of bunch that happened her (as she

was as great as ones fist, and it was not fleshy or soft, but rather stiff and
hard as a bone, which grew (as it seemed unto her) even out of the shoulder
bone, yet not having any different color from the other parts of her body,
neither was it any whit paineful, but only when she pressed it, and then
somtymes it happened that she cast blood out of her mouth The which she
sustained (without applying any remedy thereunto) about one year and a half.
But when she had heard of the miracles which were done at Moutaigu by the
invocation of our lady, she began to have a desire to go thither in

August 1603. where she did her devotion in the Chapel of our Lady, from
thence she went to lodge at Sichen, which is distant a little half duitche mile
from that place, where she perceived that her accident began to wax better: and
the next morning returning to Montaigu, whiles she was there at her prayers,
she felt certain stretchings and straynings from her head to her right arm,
and toward the place where her bunch did grow: but being that day returned to
Louaine, the next morning as she arose she found ^^r accide^t wholly cured and
the bunch to have become of the-same ^^e^nes with the other parts of her
body, so that there was no difference thereby at al, and from that time she
has re^^ained without all pain or whatsoever accide^t, as the said Religious
woman avouched in the presence of her Mother or superior and others of the
said Convent, unto whom the evil which the-sayd sister sustained, and from
which she was now freed, was well known: and likewise in the presence of the
Venerable Fathers in God sir James van Ghele Priest and Doctor of Divinity,
and Sir James de Bee^ d'Oesterwijck, also Bacheler in Divinity, and Religions
in the Convent of the Iacobins in Louain and of M. Roland l^ Prince: Secretary
of the said City, upon the xxviijth. of October 1603. and upon the vjth. of
January 1604, according to an act that by the said Secretary le Prince was
framed hereof,

How a man that was sick of the falling evil was cured.
MAtia Pacgen son of Gaspar Pacgen ^n Aug. 1603.
of Herbagh borne at S. Lauren^berg in Cuntrie of Iuliers, near unto,
Ald^n-ho^^^, came unto Montaigu in the beginning of August 1603. to make there
his petition to our Lady, that by her intercession he might be freed from the
disease and infirmity of the falling sickness, wherewith for seven years past
he had been troubled, for that he had understood that our Lord did many
miracles at the invocation of his holy Mother in that place. And so remaining
some eight or te^ days at the said Mountain, he made his prayers deuoutely
before the Chapel of our Lady: during which time he was assailed six or seven
times every da^ (as accustomarily he was wount to have been) with three sorts
or kinds of the falling evil: with such a rage and vehemency, with such
knocks hurling and cries, that every one thought he would have been burst, or
that he should have dyed, which was a most pitiful sight unto all the Pilgrims
that were there present: who also endeavored by their prayers and alms to
obtain of God his cure and amendment. And upon the eve of the Assumption of
our Lady in the said month of August, this Mathias perseuering in his prayers
and devotions, found himself in perfect health and quyte delivered from all
these maladies: in such sort that the next day every one might manifestly see,
that not only he was delivered from his falling sickness, but that there
withal he had recovered a fair and lively color in his face, which before
was very dead and pale, and his bo^^e much swollen, as many who had seen him at
Montaigu while he had his disease, and afterward when he was healed, affirmed.
Thus the said Mathi^s returned in good plight to his hows by Alden^^uen. And in
the beginning of February in the year 1604. he repaired an other time to
Montaigu, to render tha^cks unto God and his glorious Mother for the benefit
which he had there obtained, wherewith at yet he continues most certain and
assured. Afterward (to wit, upon the xiiij. of the said month) he returned
thither once again, and brought with him the attestation concerning his
maladies given him by the Curace of Alden^ ^uen, and also by the Magistrates of
the Imperial City of ^ken, dated upon the xviij. of the aforesaid month of
February, and subsigned Nicolaus Munsterus Secretary and sealed with the seal
of the same City.

Of a spice of Leprosy which was there cured.
Matthew Croisier son to Reynold Croisier In Aug. 1603.
dwelling in the town of Huy in the Cuntrie of Liege, being about twelve
years old, in the year 1603. became so full of scabbes and botches running
down along his body, that by the Curate and Curch-wardens of Saint Steuens
Parish in the same town, he was presented before the Magistrates of Huy, for a
leper, and hereupon they made him to be more diligently serched in the City of
Li^ge, to the end that if he were found a leper indeed they might provide for
him some necessary entertainment, and so to separate him from the company
and conversation of other men.

For which cause the Magistrates appointed that they should deliver him as from
the town, a bushel of corn for his food, until such time as they were fully
informed of his malady. In the mean while this youth was visited by M. Thomas
d'O^^^i^, and master Ni^^l^^ de (...) Surgeo^s of the said City, who found
him full of botches, scabbes, and deep sores, wherein he had no feeling at all:
and yet could they not certainly judge what evil it was: as appears by the
attestation of the-sayd Magistrates given under their s^al^ upon the xvij. of
Ia^uarie 1604. But the father of this youth having been in Pilgrimage at
Montaigu, and having seen and known the miracles which were there done by the
invocation of the glorious Virgin Marie, he caused his son to be brought
thither, in hope to find there some help for him, and this was about the
midst of August in the year 1603. Now as the youth was carried round about
the Chapel of our lady he began to cry out, that he was burned within his
body, and after they had ended their devotions, they carried him in-to a booth
or cottage hard by, where he rested very quietly that night, and in the morning
they found some of his botches healed, and all his soars and holes shut up,
and continuing there his denotions, within two or three days all his other
soare^ and botches of his body were ^^red of themselves, nothing remaining
but certain red spots as large as half a philip daller, and those were to
the number of forty or fifty. Moreover this youth was broken in such sort,
that his secret parts were swollen as big as both ones fi^ts: of which rupture
he was also cured at that time, without any human help or assistance: and
here of many persons of credit who were then at Montaigu do bear good
testimony, and namely M. James de Castr^ Doctor of di^initie, Archpriest or
dean of the Christianity in Die, Sir John Ha^egreaf Curate of Testel^,
Master Io^chim B^scher Secretary of the Counsel of Brab^^^, Peter de Ham
Notarie, residing at Die, and John Baptist Zangre sworn Printer in the City
of Lou^in^, of which persons some visited the young ma^n^s naked body, and
considered the perfection of his said cure, with the s^a^res that remained. And
the same young man coming afterward to Bruxelles, was visited by a skilful
Surgeon, and found whole, and quyte delivered of his rupture, and from all
other diseases whatsoever.

The Palsy Cured.
LEonard Tee^ers dwelling at Beri^gen in In Aug. 160^.
the Cuntry of Li^ge was sick of the Palsy, and so taken in all his limbs,
that he could move none of them, but only his head and tongue: the which
having continued thus a year and a half, fynding no help in any of the
receiptes or medicines which were employed for his ^ure, and being at the
length advertised of the miracles which were wrought at Montaigu, he resolved
to cause himself to be carried thither, having great confidence to find some
help by the ^ntercession of the glorious Virgin Ma^ie. The which he performed,
and was carried thither in a wagon wherein he was to be taken up and laid down
even as a very infant: when he had finished his devotion at the chapel of our
Lady, he caused himself to be carried home back again, in the same wagon,
without perceiving as ^et any amendment, but some two or three days after, he
began to move his limbs and to creep upon his hands and feet about the how^.
An other time after that he had a great desire to go again to visit our Lady
at Mo^taigu wherefore he caused a wago^ to be prepared for him, and he had now
recovered so much strength that he could go from his hows to the place where
the wagon was, and having the second time do^ne his devotion unto our Lady, he
obtained so much ease, that he left there one of his crutches, and with the
other and the help of the wagon he returned home, in better disposition, and
with more force then he had before. But fifteen days after he came thither
again the third time, and walked thither on foot only with one crutch and
seiour^ed at Montaigu for the space of fifteen days, doing there his daily
devotions: and returned home again with his crutch, but with more strength and
in better health and disposition of his body then the two times before: and
since he has every day found more ease and amendment. All this that has here
been said this Leonard Pee^ers declared and testyfied upon the xvth of August
1604. in the presence of Sir Godfrey of Thi^nwinkele Curate of Sichen, Sir John
Rosa Prior of the Iacobins in Loua^^e and Licentiate in Divinity, Brother
William Sil^ius procurator of the same Convent, Master Anthony Bouckhout
Maier of Sichen and John Baptist Zangre Printer: as also afterward he avouched
the same under his oath solemly made before the Eschoutet, Maier and Escheuins
of the aforesaid town of Beringen, as it may be seen by their attestation
sealed with their seal, and subsigned Heuricus Cillemus secretary.

The Healing of a certain disease called the Scurutes.
Elizabeth Vander Hoeuen wife unto In Aug. 1^0^.
Zacharias van A^roy, dwelling in the village of Grasen near to Bets in the
territory of Die, was in the lent 1603. taken with an accide^t and malady
which bred great pricki^gs in every part of her body, together with many black
spots of the bigness of a phillip daler whereby she became no^ only so weak
and impotent that she could do no manner of work but, more over she had such
vehement pain that she could rest neither night nor day so that she did
nothing but run out of her bed and presently run thither back again, as if
she had been deprived of her wits: yet called she continually upon the name
of the blessed Virgin Marie, to the end she would pray for her in this her
affliction: which continued until August, in the said year of our Lord 1603.
And then having hard some speak of the miracles which were wrought at Montaigu,
by the intercession of the Mother of God, she devoutly resolved to make a
pilgrimage to that place, the which she performed* and praying at the Chapel
of our Lady, immediately as she had ended her prayers, she felt a great
amendment, and that the foresaid prickings and stingings ceased: and from that
time forwards she began to be better: whereupon she was moved to return again
unto Montaigu to render thancks to the Virgin Marie, for the help she received
by her means, after which journey (being very soon after the other) the same
Elizabe^^ went home in perfect health and strength, and became so strong and
able of body, in so much as she affirmed that she never felt her self better
in all her life. According to her attestation of all the premises which
iuridicallie passed before the Eschoutet and men of law of the foresaid
Lordship of Grasen upon the thirteenth of March 1604.

How a maid was healed of her legs that were swollen and full of pain.
MArtha Vander Tay being of two and In Aug. 26 0^.
forty years of age, maid servant in the hows of M. John Va^den Petre Clarck
in the Counsel of Brabant in Bruxelles: had a disease and accide^t in her
legs, which hapened her in the year 1603, whereby they became very great and
swollen, and so full of ache that she could do no kind of labor, yea she could
not so much as go without extreme grief and shedding of tears, neither could
she repose in the night through the veheme^cie of her pain which never
stinted: but continued for the space of more then three months. Her Master
being desirous to help her, ^sed the counsel of a certain Physician dwelling
in the said City, and afterward of certain other men and women practitioners
in physic: and they appointed her a number of diverse receip^o^, as of bathes,
fomentations, ointments and other such like, but all in vain and without any
help at all. Whereupon her said master (seeing her past hope to be cured, and
that if she were cu^t she should remain a cripple, and miserable all the
residue of her life, as not able any ways to gain her living) entered into a
deliberation to place her and to provide for her in some Hospital, where she
might be maintained. But when the fame of the miracles of our Lady at Montaigu
began to be bruited abroad, he resolved at the last to send her thither, hoping
that there she might be helped. And so about mid August she was sent by wagon
to a Cloister called Te^Ba^ck near to the City of Lo^^in, wherein a sister of
the said Clark lived: and from thence also by wagon she was conveyed to Die,
that the next morning after she might go to Montaigu. In which voyage this
Martha began already to find some ease in her legs. Having rested one night in
Die, she made her self ready in the morning to go on foot unto Montaigu,
but it seemed unto her a thing impossible, and so she stood in a doubt what she
might do: which when the wife of the hows where she lodged perceived, she bad
her be of good courage, and exhorted her to go not only on foot, but barefoot
also, for that there was but one good mile to the place, which seemed unto the
said Martha a thing altogether out of her power: not withstanding being much
animated by the woman exhortation, and with the hope which she gave her that
the Mother of God would not permit her to return without comfort, on she se^^
forward barefoot, and as she went, she bega^to feel that her legs waxed
better and better. And being arrived at our Ladies chapel whylst she was at
her prayers, she felt all the swelling and pains of her legs and feet to
cease and quite to be go^, even as if one should feel some thing to be untied
and loosed which before was bound and made fast: and when her prayers were
ended she returned again barefoot unto Die, being whole and maruelously
comforted: and from Die by wagon she went back to Louain, and so to
Bruxelles fynding herself very well in all her body, as she is now even at this
present. And all this that here has been set down, was verified and avouched by
herself, under her oath solemnly made before those of the law in the said City
of Bruxelles, upon the xxvith* of April 1604. as may be seen by their
attestation given hereof, subsigned Numan, and scaled with the said Cities
seal.

A marvelous cure of an incurable wound.
LEonard Stock^^an born at S. Georges, in In Sept. 160^.
the territory of the town of H^y in the country of Liege, about some fourteen
year ago as he trauayled one day through the forest of Seign^ near to a village
called ^aterl^^s not far from Bruxelles, was assailed by a thief and murderer:
who handled him so cruelly, and gave him so many wounds, that he left him for
dead in the place: and amongst others he gave him a gash on the left hamme, in
such sort that he cut in sunder his sinews, and it passed even to the bone.
In this case was he brought to an Hospital in Bruxelles, that there he might be
seen unto: and within a certain time al his wounds were healed save that of
his hamme, the which because the sinews were cut, every one esteemed as
incurable, wherefore being dismissed out of the Hospital he was forced to go
with two crutches: yet through the abundance of humors, which somtymes had
thither their course there ensued many new sores and issues round about the
principal wound: and although he used diverse medicines of certain Physicians,
yea and had performed diverse pilgrimages, yet he found no help at all. At the
last in the month of September 1603. he went to visit our ladies at Montaigu:
where having continued nine days, and daily washing his sores with a certain
water that is in that mountain not far from the chapel, he found that the
lesser sores cured of themselves, and when the nine days were expired, he
perceived that the cut and interessed sinews of his leg, were grown and made
fast within to the bone of his said leg, and that they were round about covered
with flesh, and ^^ew skin: yet the place of the great wound remained hollow,
and with so great a hole, that one might easily put his fist therein. And thus
this Loonard was perfectly cured, without any impediment or grief, walking,
going and assisting himself, with the said leg even as he himself pleased, and
as any other man that is whole and sound might do: having afterward made on
foot the way betwixt Montaigu and Louain, which is du^tche ^iles.
five good long miles, and this he did in the month of October next following.
All which the said Stockneau declared and affirmed under a so emn oath which he
made before the Curate Ma^er and Escheuins of Siclen the xxith. of April, 1604.
according to an instrument ^ormed thereof, signed ^. ^an Ogernen Secretary,
and sealed with the seal of the said town.

How an old man was cured of the falling evil.
G^les Libens being seventy years of age dwelling at Attenhouen by the In
Sept. 160^.
town of Landen in Bra^ant, was ^exed with the falling ^uil above fifty years
together, and he was torm^^ted therewith especially upon Sundays and
Hollydayes, having but little ease of it upon other days. This aged man being
moved by the miracles wrought at Mo^taigu, purposed with himself to go thither
in Pilgrimage, and there to entreat the blessed Virgin to obtain for him that
he might be healed: the which he performed upon the seventh of September in the

subsigned Nicolaus Nicola^ Secretary, and sealed with the seal of the said
Lordship.

How a man was healed of a rupture
John Hagels Carpe^ter dwelling at Ade^oort In Sept. 1603.
by Heylihsem, near Tilem^nt, in Brabant, being threescore and four years
old, in the year 1602, and in the month of August travailing in reaping of

was inwardly built by overmuch labor: whereupon ensued a very great and
excessive pain; which continued a whole year, notwithstanding that he had
aplied many remedies in vain, at the last having hard of the miracles of our
Lady at Montaigv, and how by her intercession diverse had been healed of the
like accident, he went thither with great devotion and confidence, upon the
eight of September 1603, being the feast of the Na^iuit^e of our lady, and
having made his prayers at the Chapel, he found much ease of his pain, for
which cause within some weeks after he returned twice thither again, and at
the third time he found himself perfectly cured of his Rupture: and leaving
there his trusse wherewith he was accustomed to ty hiself, he never after felt
a^^ the least pain or hinderance thereby. As under his sole^n oath he avouched
(being summoned thereunto before the Curate, Maier and Escheuins of the Vilage
of Neder heylighse^, upon the eleventh of February 1604. according to their
attestation subsigned Seruatius Rosi^s Curate, G^^^la^^^e van Meeusele Maier,
