How a Religious woman was cured of the Cancker.
SIster Margarit va^den Perre born in Antwerp In Oct. 1601.
and there professed a lay sister in the Cloister of the third order of S.
Francis, being thirty years old, had the cancker in her breasts, for the
space of four months, as diverse Physicians and Surgeons judged, who had her
in cure: to wit, two men, and two women, and yet she could not find any help
for all their labor: yea on the contrary her evil waxed daily greater and
wors: in such sort that all those that visited her said plainly that it was
incurable, for that the patient had her breasts as hard as a stone, reddish,
bluish, and so ugly that it was a grievous thing to behold them. Her right pap
was swollen even unto her arme-pit and from thence her grief passed unto her
back, where it seemed that it would have burst out. Under the other pap was a
great swel ling, and out of her nip^^es issued somtymes a certain kind of
matter, somtymes very blood, and so it did somtymes also out of her ears.
Thus the poor Religious woman was so full of pain, and in so miserable an
estate, that for a whole years space before her cure she was not able to do
any manner of woork, neither could she ly, but was constrained to sleep
sitting, and that with very great pain: and sometimes one of her arms became
so stiff that she could not lift it to her head. And to be healed of this
accide^t she repaired to a skilful woman called Magdalen, dwelling in the
Brestraet in the said City of Antwerp: who for the space of some six months
took in hand to cure her, applying certain plasters of herbs unto her: but
when in steed of helping her she became wors, she left that cunning woman, and
used a certain plaster which a famous Surgeon dwelling the town of Harentals
called M. Peter, had prescribed her, who also helping her nothing thereby, and
perceiving her self to be past all hope to be cured, she left him also.
Afterward an old Portuguez Surgeo^, called Vento Rodriguez counseled her to
make an issue in her arm, to draw out thereby the humor of the canker: but all
was in vain, and to no profit at all. After that again she applied diverse
remedies which some of her neighbors and friends taught her, but without any
further success. After a certain time she permitted that her breasts might be
visited by an elderlie maid, who exercised her self in surgerie called Anne
Cammarts, alias A^^c^^^x: who having visited her twice or thryce, and
perceiving that her disease was incurable: she gave her no other cou^ sell, but
that she should take a purgation twice or thryce every year: which she tried
for once or twice, but durst not proceed therein, in regard of an other
accident which she had, to wit, a rupture, which also she had sustained for
the space of viij years. At the last she showed her impediment again to an
other cunning woman called Gertrude Munters, who found that the canker was not
only in both her breasts, but that it had passed even unto her back, where
also she felt a great hardness: and this woman did nothing else to her but rub
her back with a certain kind of ointme^t, which she could hardly endure,
causing her to apply unto her breasts certain places of lead, and fair
lin^en, counseling her furthermore to tamper with no more physic, but to
commend all unto God, for so much as there was no other way to help her. And in
this manner this Religious woman was abandoned and forsaken of all human
help, every one foretelling her that visited her that e^e long she should come
to that misery that would be most lamentable for any to b^hold. In this time
so vehement and excessive great were the pains which this Religious woman and
^red, that often times she consumed whole nights in tears and lamenting.

But some three months after having understood that Sister Ann^d B^urn, the
Cla^^sse was miraculousely cured by the invocation of our Lady of Montaigu, she
turned her self with all her ha^t toward our lady, beseeching the mother or
superior of the Conue^t that she might make a voyage to Montaigu, to recommend
there her health unto the Mother of God.

Which was granted her, upon the fourth day of November in the year 1603: and
from the very time that she had obtained her said leave, she began to feel some
ease in her self. And upon the next day she departed from An^werp, together
with Sister Marie Clements, guardian of the sick, who had assisted her during
the time of her malady. They having past by Bruxelles and arrived at Lo^ain
the patient being not able to endure the shoggig of the waggo^, went from
Louain unto Montaigu on ^oot. Whether when they were come, they did their
devotions that very day in the Chapel of our Lady. The next day (being the
nynth of the aforesaid month) they hard three masse^, at the first mass the
said patient was very weak and sick, but having received the blessed Sacrament
of the altar she began to feel in herself a notable ease, as well in regard of
her disease of the cancker as of her rupture, and at the third mass she found
herself perfectly whole: for it s^emed unto her that she felt a hand stroki^g
over her and therewith to wype away all her pain. And from that time feeling
herself perfectly whole, she gave thancks to God, and to his most holy Mother,
leaving in the Chapel the lead and clothes which she used before. And thus
returned with her company to Antwerp whole and sound. And being come home,
the said sister Marie (...) visited her breasts, and fosid them perfectly cured
and in good order: where as before they were so miserable and deformed, that
none could behold them without horror: fynding also that the end of her teat
was closed up, and that there was no hardness in all her bosom but a very
little in her left pap, which within three or four days after was gone and
ceased.

So that since, the time of this visitation she remained q^yre delivered and
free of the c^cker, as also of her rupture, which she had endured for eight
years space, as has been said: and so she settled herself to labor and
travail ^gaine with the other Religious in the said Cloister, as before she
was accustomed. Some days after her return she was visited again as well by the
aforesaid An^e Cammarts, as also by Gertrude Man^ers, both expert in forgerie
as we have said, who to their great admiration found the said Religious
intyrely and perfectly cured, as well in her breasts, as in her arme-pitts and
back, without any appearance or sign of any hardness, or of any other disease,
but that she was whole, and very well in all her body. All this here set down
was affirmed and verified by their solemn oaths, made in the hands of the
aforesaid Vicare of Antwerp, upon the xxj. of November 1603, and upon the iiij.
of December in the same year. The like solemn attestation was made thereof
before these commissaries: M. John vander Noot Escheuin, and M. Denis va^der
N^esen secretary of the said City, by these persons here named: to wit, by
Sister Ioane de Herd Mother ^r Superior of thesavd Convent, by the fore*
named Sister Marga^^t vander Perre, Sister Marie Clemens, mistress or guardian of
the infirmarie, Sister Hester de Mompere, and Sister Marie Perez, all Religious
women of the same Convent: who at sundry times had assisted this Sister
Marga^^t, and had seen her diseases, who also knew her repture, whereof
together with her cancker she was healed, as has binsayd. Also the aforesaid
An^e Camm^erts alias Abacucx and Ge^^^le Man^ers affirmed the same under their
oaths: who in times past had care of the said Religious woman, and had visited
her breasts, both before and after her said cure, as is manifest by an
instrument framed thereof, and dated as above.

The curing of a sore which was sisteen years old.
IOane Rut^ the widow of Io^n St^obant, in Nou. 1603.
of about fifty years of age, dwelli^g in the lordship of Campenhout in the
Maierdome of the City of B^^xell^s. In the year 1589. got an accident in her
left leg, upon the ankle of her soot, whereupon grew a sore or issue as great
in compass as ones h^nd, and a finger or more in length: wherein she felt such
vehemen^ and continual pain, that she could neither by night or day take any
rest: and she was very often fully minded to have cut of that leg, b^^ing
forced for the most part to keep her bed, or to sit in a chair, being not able
to go in any manner, except it were sometimes with two crutches, or whith a
staff, or else creeping on all four upon the ground. And although she had
applied diverse remedies, yet could she receine no ease, and her cuil was
acounted incurable. But in the year 1603. hauig hard of the miracles which o^r
Lord did woork by the invocation of his ho^y Mother at Montaigu the said Ioane
made a vow to go thither in pilgrimage: and whereas through her great pain,
debilitie, and weakn^ she was not able to go, it happened that a certain person
moved with compassion of her estate, carried her in a wagon unto Montaigu, in
the month of October in the aforesaid year 1603. Where being in the Chapel
of our Lady she did there her devotions, with firm hope and confidence to be
cured: and returuing hom^ carried with her some of the water which is behynd the
chapel in the said Mountain, the which (that it might last the longer) thee
mixed with r^uer water, and she daily washed and made clean her l^g there
with, whereby incontinently she perceived a great alte^ation and e^se in her
sore, and without applying any thing else thereunto it healed up of it self, and
with^n few months was perfectly whole, in ^uch sort that at this present she
goes and walks lustely whethersoeuer she pleases, not feeling any pain or
grief* being now able to go three or four duitche miles at a time, whereas
before (though she might thereby have gained all the world) she was not able to
go one mile. And in thankfulness for this benefit, the said Ioane went an other
time in Pilgrimage to Montaigu, within the Octaues of the Assu^p^ion of our
Lady, in this year 1604. and this she performed on foot, and went thither on
one day, and returned on the next, without any impediment by her former
accident. As the said Ioane declared and avouched all these things under her
oath, solemnly given before the chief Maier and Escheuines of the said Lordship
of Campenh^ut, upon the nynteenth of October in the said year 1604, according
to their attestation given thereof, and sealed with the seal of the said
Lordship, and subsigned R. Hermans Secretary.

How a Child being broken was cured.
FRancis Addiers of four years and an Ir Nou. 1603.
half old, the son of Francis Addiers, and of Annevande^ VVinckele his wife
dwelling in Bruxelles, was broken on the left side of his belly, and this
happened him when he was but six weeks old, so that from that time they made him
wear a trusse, because the said rupture appeared of the bigness of a turkeys
egg, and never kept in, but when they put on his trusse: and often times it
was seen in his secret parts, whereby he endured great pain, especially twice
or thrice every month at the change of the moon. And although his mother had
applied diverse medicines both by the advice of some surgeons as of others, yet
she nothing prevailed.

But having heard the fame of Montaigu, and of the miracles that were there
wrought by the in^ocation of our Lady, she resolved to carry thither her
child, and there to pray unto our Lady for his health, which she performed
about the midst of October, in the year 1603, and remained there for three
days, praying daily in the said Chapel: and after the third day she
perceived that her chylds disease was much amended. Whereupon she left there
his trusse in memory thereof: and being come home she perceived that his
rupture appeared again but after that time her child was perfectly cured, so
that since the said pilgrimage he never needed either tr^sse or any other
remedy, being much altered in his body, so that he became fatter and
stronger, going, running, and playing, as other children of his age are wou^t
to do, not feeling any pain or impediment by the said drupture: which things
his mother sole^nly affirmed under her oath, in the presence of the Magistrates
of Bruxelles, upon the eleventh of December, in the said year 1603. Upon which
day also Arnold Addiers under burgemaister of the said city declared and
affirmed under the like oath before the said M^gistrates, that he had seen the
said child thus broken, when he was but six weeks old, as has been said: and
that he had made inquiry after all sorts of remedies to cure him, if it had
been possible, and yet nothing would help, so that the surgeons were of opinion
that the child was to be cut, whereunto neither he nor any of his kins^olks
and friends would agree, showing more over that he knew right well how that the
said A^^^ vanden Winkele his daughter in law went with the said child to visit
our Lady a^ Montaigu, and how that after her return the said child was found
to be cured, as now he is. And all this is manifest by the attestation of the
Magistrates, subsigned P. Numan, and sealed with the scale of the same City.

A sudden cure of a laguishing disease:
SIster Michielle Blyleuen, daughter of M. In No^. 1603.
Thomas Blyleuen Sergeant Ma^or of the City of Louain, professed Religious of
the Convent of the Annunciata in the said City, in the year 1603 fell into a
great disease, which lasted for the space of six months, together which a
perpetual pensiuenes at her heart, and a shortness of breath; which was so great
that she lost all her strength, being so feeble and faint, that six or seven
times every day the swear issued violently out of every part of her body, and
the tears out of her eyes; and for two whole months she was not able to go in
any sort, but as she was led by some one of the Religious, at which time she
so lost her appetite, that she would receive no meat, but upon force and her
superiors commaundment. In such sort, that she was forced to use the counsel
first of Doctor Vilerius, and afterward continually of Doctor Fienus both
professors of Physic in the University of Louain. But for all that they had
prescribed her receiptes at diverse times, yet she found no profit or ease
thereby. Whereupon having now for two months space left all use of Physic,
she determined to go and pray three times at the Chapel which they had
accomodated in their garden, in the honor of our lady, and in memory of the
miracles which by her intercession were wrought at Montaigu: with a desire to
have done the same in the place it self if it might have been permitted her.
Going therefore to the said Chapel, with great pain and labor, upon a
saturday being the xvth. of November in the said year 1603: and having there
do^ne her devotion, she began to feel a great ease and alteration in her body,
recovering a notable force and ablenes in her self, in so much that on the same
day she did read the mattines of our Lady on her knees, which for five months
before she was not able to do. On the night following she being in the quier
with the rest of the religious, and reading her hours, at the very instant
that mattines was ended by the song of Salve Regina, the said Sister Michielle
felt as it were a hand upon her shoulder which seemed to have pressed her down,
and this was in so evident a manner that she felt and perfectly discerned the
very fingers; whereby she started, and looked back to see the person that
touched her. After Mattines she went to repose her, and rising again in the
morning she found herself meruelously amended, and so strong, that immediately
after, she went to the Church to be present at divine service with the rest of
the Religious, with whom she sung so loud and lively that they were greatly
astonished thereat, not knowing what voice it was that sounded so shrill. And
from that time afterward she has remained healthie, and in good plight,
singing and assisting at the ordinary obseruances as the other Religious: who
a^ouch and testify, that they never saw her so strong and in so good lyking as
she has been since the time above mentioned. And the Superior and Vicaresse
of the said Convent have given attestation and certified under their seals,
that all this is true that has been here related. Likewise the said religious
has also affirmed the same in the hands of the Reverend Father Antonie de
Bergaigne their ghostly father, upon the twentieth of Ianuarte 1604, and after
that again in the presence of the Magistrates of the said City of Louain upon
the xvj. of March in the said year 1604. Upon which day also the said
Superior Sister Clare van Leyden appearing before the same Magistrates,
declared that she knew very well that the said Religious was so long time sick,
and in the aforesaid plight, as having seen it partly with her own eyes, and
partly having understood so much from the said Religious herself, as it is to be
seen by the attestation subsigned R. de Prince Secretary, and sealed with the
seal of the same City.

The cure of a rupture.
FRancis de Alarcon one of the house hold In Nou. 1603.
of the most gracious Archdukes Albert and Isabel Dukes of Brabant our Princes,
happened to be inwardly broken in managing and conducting a froward and
stubborn horse, and the rupture came forth as big as ones fist, who having
endured this evil with much pain for three years and an half, and having used
diverse remedies, by ba^ds, trusses, as other wise, yet without any proffit: at
last he went in pilgrimage to our Ladies at Montaigu, where having prayed a
while in the Chapel, he found himself perfectly freed and healed of his
Rupture: inso much as be left of his band or trusse which he had worn before,
as appears by his attestation given under his own seal.

How a wench that had the palsy, and was deprived of her wits was healed.
ANgela wouters daughter of Elizabeth In No^. 1603.
van Herp the wife of Mathias Le^teens cooper, dwelling in the old Corne-market
in the City of Antwerp, about thirteen years old, was in the month of
September 1603. attained with a certain kind of Apoplexy, especialy in her
arms, and in her right side and leg, with so great a stretching and tremblyng
that she could not go, and at certain times she became dumme, in such sort
that none could understand her when she indcuoured to speak. At last she wholly
lost her speech besides this, she was deprived of her wits, and became so
weak, that she could not apparel herself, no nor so much as put her meat into
her mouth. Her parents caused Master Bennet Rutten sworn Doctor of ^hysick for
the City of Antwerp to be sent for, who visiting the maid, let her blood in
the foot, and afterward gave her a purge, for he was of opinion that her
malladie proceeded of some interior motion, which Physicians call Motus
con^ulsi^^* which take their beginning of some venomous m^^ter gathered in the
brain: but after he had visited her twice or thrice, he let her parents
sufficiently to understand that he had little hope of her recovery, counseling
them to ma(...) some pilgrimage (...) to ^se some other kind of devotion wi^^
their child, and to call upon the help o^ God for her. Which when her parents
had heard they resolved that one of them should go with her to Montaigu, there
to salute the Vi^gin Marie and this was to be performed so soon as the winter
was past. But upon the xxj. of November (being the feast of the Presentation
of our Lady) the said Mathias rising in the morning* advertised his wife of
the feast, and counseled her to go with her daughter to our Ladies Church in
the said City of Ant^erp, to hear mass, and to pray there for her health:
which she did, and after she had heard mass she bought a wax taper,
commanding her daughter to light it, and to set it on the candlestick which
stands before our Ladies altar, which she did with the hand that had the
palsy, assisting and lifting it up with the other hand, her mother beseeching
God to help her, and the blessed Virgin to pray for her health, exhorting her
daughter to call upon the Mother o^ God, that she would vouchsafe to pray for
her: and immediately the said candle (although it was very well lighted) went
out of it self. Beei^g the second time lighted, out it went again, as it
happened also (...) third time, vet she caused it still to b(...) (...)ed again,
and that the maid by her (...) should put it on the foresaid candlestick,
persuading herself that it would be a thing right pleasing to the Virgin Marie
that the child herself should offer up the candle unto her. This done, home
she returns with her daughter, fynding for all this no alteration that day
in the maid: but the wench arising the next day (being the two and twe^tith of
the said month) early in the morning, down she comes all apparailed, whereat
her Mother was much abashed, and enquired of her who had apparailed her: and
when she had heard her answer that she alone had do^ne it, and on the other
part seeing her daughter to go so perfectly well, she began to thanck God and
his holy Mother for it, being singulerly glad to see in her this alteration.
And from that day still afterward the said wench remained whole and sound,
going, speaking, and performing all her bodily functions as well as ever she had
do^ne before: Where as during her foresaid disease she was never able to put on
her clothes, to walk, to speak, or to do any kind of work, but she sat always
trembling, and drawing in her limbs, and sometimes for the space of three
days together a great quantity of froathie spettle ran continually out of
her mouth. And the aforesaid M. Bennet Rutten coming some certain days after
to visit the maid, found her sudda(...) healed as has been said. And all that
(...) bee^ here related is to be seen by them formation taken hereof upon the
fifteenth as also upon the last of December, in the said year 1603. by M. John
vander Noot esquire and Escheuin, and Master Denis vander Neesen Secretary of
the said city of Antwerp, appointed by Magistrates in commission for this
matter. Who upon these things examined under their solemn oaths the said
Mathias Lesteens her Father in law, and Elizabeth van Herp her Mother, the
aforesaid Doctor Master Bennet Rutten, and with these Father Michel van
Ophouen licentiate in Divinity, and Religious in the Cloister of the Iacobins
in the same place, who was kinsman to the child, and had also seen her first
sick, and afterward miraculously cured.

The cure of a Rupture.
Master Balthazar ^an Rossum esquire, ^^ ^ou. 1603.
sometimes coronel of a (...)ent of Allemans in the king or S(...) ^ service,
being of the age of eight ^^^ fifty, in the year 1597. as he was in the
City of Luxemburg he found himself burst on the left side, the which accident
he caused to be visited by diverse surg^ons, both in the said City of
Luxemburg, as also afterward in the City of Do^ay, who judged it to be a very
Hernia or Rupture: and after he had used diverse helps and remedies, at last he
was constrained to wear a trusse fitted for the purpose, not knowing any other
wa^ whereby, to he^p himself. But in the year 1603. ha^ing heard of the
miracles of our la^ie at Mo^taig^ he made a secret promis to go thither in
pilgrimage, and to pray for his health, with good hope to find there some help
and favor. And he accomplished this his devout voyage thryse, about the month
of September in the foresaid year, and after a while one day in Bruxell^s
taking of his trusse which he used to wear, he found himself perfectly healed,
never having any feeling thereof afterward, verily assuring himself that he
had obtained the said cure, only by the favor of God which he had found in
thesayd pilgrimage: for so he declared and avouched the ^ame under his so^^ne
oath upon the xth of Iulie, in the hands of M. John Briex Notarie in the City
of Bruges, and in the presence of Andrew Vermeulen, and George the son of
George Modan witnesses: as appears by a public instrument dispatched
hereof, dated and signed as above, together with the subscript o^ of the said
van R^ssum, with his own hand.

How a Religious woman was suddenly cured of a strange and incurable disease.
SIster Barbara de Berges, the daughter of I^ D^^^ 1^03
M. Gerard de Berges in his lyfe-tyme Physician of Antwerp, being six and
thirty years old, made her profession in Religion in the Cloister called of
the sick lea^ers in the said City, where she was taken with a grievous
malladie, which forced her to keep her bed continually for the space of six
years and three months. Of this her disease no man could give any judgment
what it should be, some saying as mamely D. Ema^^el G^mez Portugues (after that
he had applied unto her many remedies) that it was an inward cancker. Others as
M Bennet Rutten sworn Physician of the said City, that it was Melancholia
hypochondriaca, proceeding from the spleen and left side, accompained with
diverse other accidents and infirmities, as the beating of the heart, and a
certain kind of anguish which took her so often as any person touched her
body, though never so little: and this with such a faynting and feeblenes, that
it seemed that death it self would immediately have ensued thereof. In so-much
that they could not past twyse or thryse in a year take her out of her bed:
and yet every time she would fall into such qualmes and fayntings that they
thought she would have dyed, and at one time amongst others being taken out of
her bed, and laid upon an other on the ground, until such time as her own was
made ready, she became so feeble by this touching and removing her, that they
were forced to let her so ly on the ground for fifteen days continually before
she could return again to her self. Whereof many were witnesses, as hereafter
shallbe set down: and amongst the rest the Reverend. M. Gosu^n Ba^son Chanon of
our Ladies in An^werp, and other Religious women who had assisted in that time
of her sowning. And although she became very cold lying in this manner on the
ground, yet she could not endure that any should apply any hot napkins or
clothes to warm her body, for then would she fall again into her former
sowning and fayntings, that every one looked for nothing else but that she
should die. Yea, which is more, if any did but only touch the bed wherein she
did ly, or so much as the curtains, she took such an apprehension thereof,
that she sowned incontinently, and for this cause, they removed her out of her
bed but twice or thryse in a year, as we have declared.

And the Religious women that attended her were constrained to put good store
of thorns round about the pillars of her bed to the end that none might touch
it whereby the patient might not fall into her strange swownings. And it is to
be noted, that for the space of s^^ month; before she was healed she had never been out of her bed and she could never sit upright therein, either to eat or
drinck, or to do any thing else: moreover the sinews of her left leg were so
shru^ck up that it was shorter by a foot then the other. Again for these six
years this poor religious person had used the counsel and help of many
Physicians, and had tried many medicines, receiptes, and remedies, which rather
made her wors then better: in so much as the Physicians plainly affirmed that
they knew not how to help her. Some sower years before she was cured they made
her an issue, and they thrust a great red whote pack needle through the skin of
her left side, drawing through the same a cord made of silk, the which (for
the space of three months) they drew daily up and down to make a way, through
the which the bad humors might pass: and although hereby she suffered much
pain, yet it profited her nothing at all: yea she rather felt her self woors
then before. Now this Religious seeing there was no hope in man, she armed her
self with patience the best she could, and she had for some years before upon
devotion determined that when she had thus lain seven years, she would either
visit or cause some to visit our Lady of Hanswyck in the city of Maclin, in
hope by way of prayer to obtain her health. But in the mean while having
heard of the great miracles w^^ch were wrought at Montaigu by the invocation of
the glorious Virgin Marie, she had a great desire to visit that place, and she
b^^^eched God to afford her so much strength that she might be carried thither.
In the mean time sister A^^e va^ Calst^r Superior of that Convent having
compassion of the desolate poor creature promised her, that she her self would
go and visit our Lady at Montaigu for her, and that there she would pray for
he^ health: the which thing she fulfilled: and being returned home, she went
to see the said Religious whom she found in the self same state, who told her
Superior that she thought it good to go thither thryce and that she had
beseeched our Lord that she her self might be the third person that should
there visit our Lady. It happened not long after that the above named Chanon
Batson (who diverse times upon charity visited and comforted the patient in her
afflictions) had said mass in the said Convent: at which time he recommended
her to God, and at that very time determined to make a pilgrimage unto Montaigu
in her name, and there to pray for her health. After the mass was said he went
unto the sick person, and declared unto her his intention: the which when she
had heard, she was inwardly altered, and seemed to be exceedingly glad thereof,
as the said M. Batson well perceived: whereby he felt him self the more incited
to accomplish thesayd promise. Upon this resolution he departed from Antwerp
with Sir Vulmar^ Schetz Pastor of the said Convent, passing by bote on the
river of Scaldis unto Willebrook, from thence they went on foot unto Montaigu,
and in like manner returned back again on foot afterward. Being at Montaigu
upon the third of December, in the said year 1603. which was the eve of S.
Barbara, they both calebrated mass in the Chapel of our Lady, and prayed
unto almighty God by the intercession of his holy Mother to vouchsafe to
restore this poor and miserable Religious woman to her health. Upon the self
same day that the holy sacrifice was there offered for her, the said Religious
woman being in Antwerp in her bed felt her self to be much amended, and to
have obtained a new strength, and immediately afterward she felt so great
pain in her body, that she fell into an ague. The next day (being the feast
of S. Barbara) at eleven of the clock about noon she began again to feel her
strength much to increase, and she spoke to the Sister that kept her that she
would reach unto her her hand, which when she had taken, she raised up her
self by her self, upon her feet upon her bed: whereat the sister being much
astonished cried out for fear, and the said Religious fell down heavily again
upon her bed, not sustaining for all this any alteration or faintnes hereby,
whereas before she was wou^t to fall into sowning and that almost to death, when
any did so much as but touch her, yea although it were never so softly, as has
been said. And the said sister Barbara de Berges remained all that day in her
bed, although she thought that after dinner she was strong enough to walk up
and down her chamber. But upon the next day following which was friday and the
fifth of the aforesaid month of December, she craved to have her apparel
delivered unto her, which was given her, and she put it on alone by her self
without any to help her, beginning first with her left arm, on which side all
her disease had been, which arm none might touch before, no more then any
other part of her body without the danger of falling into her accustomed
faintenes: and so having apparailed herself she came cheerfully out of her
bed: and signing her self with the sign of the cross, down she cast herself
upon her knees, and lifting up her eyes to heaven, she gave thancks to our Lord
and said: Praise be to the O Mari^. Which when the other Religious women saw
who were in the chamber with her, they powered out tears of joy: and Sister
Michielle de Bergu^s the natural Sister of the said Barbara fell into a swoune,
upon tender affection and astonishement which she had conceived. After this the
said Sister sat her down in a chair by the fire for an hour or two, where as
before she could not endure any fire, no not so much as that her clothes should
be warmed. Sitting thus before the fy^r she said that she fe^t such a force and
strength in her bones and ma^ow, from her head down to her feet, as if some had
powered somewhat from above upon her, and she began to walk all alone about the
chamber. Whereupon the religious women who were there present sang Te Deum in
way of thancks giving, and after that the Hymn A^^ Mar^s stella, the said
patient inioying the health and good disposition of her body going and walking
up and down whether so ever she pleased recovering also her appetite which so
long time before she had lost, in so much that ^oorthwith she dranck a good
draught of wine, and some other sustena^ce she also received, and that with a
very good stomach, whereas in times past she had no desire to her meat, and
she could not so much as swallow down a little wine although it were drop after
drop without great pain and difficulty. And upon the same friday at night
came home from Mo^taigu the said master Batso^, and the Pastor, and coming
into the said religious woman's chamber, they found her sitting before the fire,
who arose incontinently of her self and gave them the welcome home, showing
unto the^ how that all her accidents and diseases were perfectly cured. And so
became daily more strong, and in better plight: in such sort, that upon the
next day she heard three masses, with the rest of the Conue^t, at the which she
assisted for the most part upon her knees. Some two or three days after the
feast of S. Barbara the a foresaid Doctor M. Benedict Rutten was sent for by
the Convent, to visit the said religious woman, whom he found whole and
strong, going up and down the monastery without any crutch, staff, or any
human help. And all this that has been here said was verified and solemnly
avouched before Master John vander N^^^ Esquire and Escheuin, and master
Denis vander N^^s^n Secretary of the said City of Antwerp appointed in
commission by the Magistrates for this matter as has been said, acording to
the information taken hereof, and put in writing: and this by diverse persons of
good: credit, who at diverse times had visited and assisted the said patient in
her grievous malladie, and afterward found her thus suddenly cured: to wit,
the said Sister Anne van Cal^^^re Superior, the said Master Gosuin Ba^son
Chanon, and Master VV^mare Schetz Pastor, the said Sister Barbara de Bergues
the said Doctor Benedict Rutten, and Sister Michielle de Bergues upon the last
of December, in the said year 1603. And this same religious was afterward in
very good and perfect health of body upon the last of May in the year 1604,
being visited by him that has written these things and in the month of Iulie
she personally went in pilgrimage to our Ladies at Mo^taigu, as she herself had
before prayed our Lord, and verily trusted that she should be the third that
was to go thither in pilgrimage for herself: a thing to all the world very
strange and wounderfull.

A long deafnes cured.
DAme Adrian de Goux de wedergraet In De^. 1603.
Prioresse of the Cloister of Shert^gi^^en dale or valley of the Duchess at
O^^^rgem near to the City of Bruxelles: some thirtie-eight years ago became
deaf or both her ears, in such sort that she could not hear when the
Riligious did sing, yea although they did all sing together in her presence,
hearing nothing but a certain little sound as if it had been a far of, and the
like was of the sound of the belles of the said Convent. Besides this* she had
an exceeding continual pain in the top of her head, with a certain noise in
her ears, as if it had been of a water-mill. And although she had applied
diverse remedies, as well by the advice of Physicians, as of others, yet she
received no benefit by them: but that sometimes after she had used these
medicines, and receiptes, she felt her self a little amended, the which lasted
for some one, two, or three months, but she fell again incontinently in to her
accustomed deafnes^ and thus passing many years therewith, she abandoned all
physic, wholly resigning herself to the will of God. But at last understanding
of the miracles of Mo^taigu she purposed to send some thither to our Lady in
pilgrimage: and about the feast of S. Remigius in the year 1603, she sent
thither M. John wa^lart a religiou^ man, and A^^onet Hazard her maid, with an
alms, and she sent thither afterward the said A^tonet alone. The which
pilgrimages being ended, it happened upon the first Sunday of Adue^t that the
said Dame Adrian having been that night at Mattines with the other religious
women: and returned thence to take her rest, she began to dream, and being
betwixt sleeping and waking it seemed unto her that she saw before her an image
of our Lady, the which opening her eyes she beheld: at which sight at the
beginning she was affraied, but taking courage she beseeched the glorious
Virgin Marie that she would vouchsate to pray for the cure of her deafnes: and
forthwith the said Image stretched forth the hand, and touched her upon the
temples and eyes, saying unto her certain words: whereof she has as yet
perfect memory. And so vanishing away, upon the next day, thesayd Prioresse
perceived that she began to hear better then before, and afterward by little
and little within the space of seven or eight days s^e perfectly recovered her
hearing: in so much as at this present she not only hears the sound of the
belles, or the song of the religious, but she can perfectly and distinctly
hear what any speaks, as well as any other, not having the former pains or
noise in her head. As the said dame Prioresse has testified and avouched all
this that here has been said under her own seal, and the seal of her
Co^ue^t, as also under their seals the like has been donn by Father John
M^lemans Confessor, Sister Marie vander Linde^ Subprioresse, Sister Elizabeth
Houture, Sister Marie Beck, Sister Elizabeth du Terne, and Sister Anneva^ Di^ue
all religious women of this Convent: who have seen and noted the said dame
Prioresse, to have had the aforesaid deafenes, and now to enjoy her perfect
hearing, according to an instrument framed thereof, subsigned and sealed as
above, upon the xxvj of May 1604.

How a lamce wench was cured.
John Nyemegens Apoticarie dwelling in In D^^^ 1603.
the Keestrate in the City of Ant^werp, had a daughter called Margarit about
thirtee^ years of age, who from the time that she was six woneths old had a
lame foot, in such sort that her right leg was shorter then the other by a
good hand breadth; whereupon they were constrained to underlay her shoe, and
make it higher, and for all this she went with great pain upon her toes, for
that her heel could not rest upon her shoe, as appeared to the commissaries
according to the information which they received thereof. This wench having
heard what was reported of the miracles which by the intercession of the
glorious Virgin Mother of God were wrought at Montaigu, she never ceased to
entreat her Father to permit her to go thither upon devotion: but her Father
telling her if she desired to be cured, that thereby she might be more pleasing
and acceptable to the world, that then infallibly her prayers would never be
granted. She answered him that she intended no such thing, but rather that her
intention was good and holy: and thereupon he yielded unto her that she might
go that voyage, sending with her an ancient maid servant, called Anne van
Poyer: and they both departed together from Ant(...)erp upon the xxv^th. of
November 1603. and arrived at Die upon the xxviijth. and then upon the next
day being the xxixth. they went to Montaigu, where they remained two days: to
win the xxxth of the said month of November, and the first of December: lying
one night at Montaigu and the other night at Sic^^^: daily performing their
devotions at the Chapel of our Lady: and upon the third day at the end of the
second mass which they hard, the said Margari^ perceived that her foot was
amended, telling the foresaid servant, that she thought she could go well enough
without her high shoe, and thereupon she began to stand upon her feet, and to
walk upright. And being returned from thence to Die they bought her an other
pair of shoes of aequal higth, which she put on, and she perceived that her
legs were now become aequal, and the one as long as the other. And thus upon
the fifth of the said month of December they returned to Antwerp, the said
Margarit being delivered from her accustomed halting, now, walking on both her
feet with shoes of equal higth, because her legs were be come of aequall
length. All which was verified and avouched under their solemn o^hes, both by
the aforesaid John Nyemegens, and by Marie Vermeulen his wife, as also by the
said Anne van Poyer, Philippes vanden Brook and John de Ram Almoner of the said
City and neighbor unto thesayd John Nyemegens, before the aforesaid M. John
vander Noo^ Esquire and Escheuin, and Master Denis vander Neesen Secretary of
the said City of Antwerp, put in commission about this affair: all which
above named persons knew this wench to have been lame even from her infancy,
and to have been miraculously cured as has been said: as in like manner
thesayd Margarit Nyemege^s declared the same in the presence of the former
persons, comformable to an information taken thereof upon the xijth. of the
said month of December 1603.

The sore eyes of a Child suddenly cured.
ELizabeth Verbiest daughter of Peter Ver^^est Sopemaker dwelling in the City
In Dec. 1603.
of Antwerp upon the Zant, and of Mari^ Speeka^rs his wife, being seven years
old, about Christmasse in the year 1603. had an accident in her eyes for the
space of five or six days, her eyes being very read and inflamed, in so much
that she could not endure the daylight nor any other light, and through the
pain thereof she could rest neither by day or by night, and one of her eyes
was swollen as big as a great nut, and although her parents ceased not to apply
diverse remedies to them, yet no amendment insued thereby. It happened that on a
certain day the chyldes mother met with one la^^ Go^arts the wife of John
Bertells a bleacher of linne^ cloth, dwelling in Antwerp, and talking with her
of the said accident, thesayd la^e gave unto her a little piece of the Oak of
our Lady of Montaigu to use it against the aforesaid disease.

Which the said mother receiving, putting her hope in the help of the Virgin
Marie she steeped the said wood in a little rose water mixed with rain water,
and a little holy water, and with this water she washed one morning her
daughters eyes, who the next night rested very well, not feeling any pain at
all, and upon the day following in the morning, she awaked as perfectly whole
and cured as ever she was before the foresaid disease had happened unto her: in
so much that she went to the school the very self same day, feeling afterward
no manner of grief in her eyes. As her father and mother avouched the same
under their oaths before the Magistrates of the City of Antwerp, upon the
nynth of March in the year 1604* according to an act framed thereof, and
subsigned Vander Neesen Secretary of the said City.

The cure of a sore that was five and twenty years old.
Anthony vande^ Velde keeper and officer In D^^. 1^03
of the forest of So^gne: dwelling in the village of Terhulp three duitch miles
^^o^ Bruxdles was attainted with a quartain ague in the year 1575. which
continued about three or four years, whereby he became so weak and lean that
he was but only skin and bones, Moreover his left leg became so great that
he was not able to walk thereon: and this having continued long, and fynding no
help although he had applied many things thereunto by the adui^e and counsel of
some apothecaries and others, upon a day as he went unto a certain surgeon in
hope to be helped by him, who intending to give some ease to the patie^t, with
a corrisiue medicin made a little hole in the said leg, whereby some water and
moisture began to issue out of the same, but nothing else: and after a while
sundry other yssues began to grow in diverse parts thereof, somtymes on the
one side sometime on the other side of that which was made by the barber. In
so much that in short time al these yssues gatheri^g into one, they made a sore
of the greatness and compass of an egg: and this upon the shinne above the
ankle, being very red, and burning ho^e, and so full of corruption that many
thought the very bone had perished and decayed. And as the patient endured
intolerable pain, he caused diverse other remedies to be applied thereunto,
but all in vain and to no purpose. He also went in pilgrimage to diverse devout
places, and yet obtained he no ease at all thereby. At the last in the year
1603. in the month of December, in the beginning of Aduent having heard some
talk of the miracles which by the intercession of the glorious Virgin Marie
were wrought at Montaigu, the said Anthony much desired to get some piece of
the wood of the Oak wherein the miraculous picture had wount to have been set:
and having by the means of a certain friend obtained a piece, and withal a
silver medall of our Lady of the same place, he put them both into cold water,
and there with he washed his sore for the space of nine days, adding some few
prayers unto God, and to the glorious Virgin Marie. And from the very time that
he began to wash his leg, he perceived that the sore (which he sustained for
fyue-and-twentie years together, with much pain weakness and extenuation of
his body) began to close up, and every day to become lesser and lesser, in
such sort that when the nine days were expired, it was quyte shut up and
healed, and since that time, he has remained in good plight, not feeling
therein any swelling or pain, declaring that from that time he has found his
body in good disposition and health, that he seems to himself to have become
younger then he was before. All which that here has been said he avouched under
his solemn oath before the Magistrates of the City of Bruxelles, upon the
xxjth. of October 1604. And upon the same day appeared also before the said
Magistrates Mistress Gertrude Ianotea^ wife of VVrbert Valle, dwelling at the
Inn called du Ken^ebutin in the same City, and with her Bertr and vanden
Velde brother and Anthonette Baston wife of the said Anthony vanden Velde, who
under the like oaths affirmed that they had often seen the said sore, the which
was very foul and ugly to behold: to wit, the said Mistress Gertrude some
eight years ago, and thesayd Anthonette ever since it first began. As also
they had seen the same sore after he had washed it, and they had found it whole
and cured as has been said: as also at that very time the said Anthony showed
it to the magistrates them selves, who found it to be intiere and whole,
according to their attestation made hereof, sealed with the seal of the said
City, and signed P. Numan Secretary, and dated as above.

The punishment of a soldier that determined to hinder the Pilgrimage of
Montaigu.
IT will not be from the purpose to declare ^n Dec. 1603.
in this place, how that a certain soldier of the gheusos and rebels of
Holland had determined one day with twelve other companions to swim over the
river of Demere, and so to come and kill such Pilgrims as went toward our Lady
of Montaigu, and there withal to rob the jewels and donaries that were offered
there. And for this purpos they had fitted themselves with certain suits of
canuas, that they might be the sooner dry. But meaning first to undertake some
other exploit with these his mates, he was wounded through both his legs by
an harquebuse, in such sort that his determination was dashed. As he himself
(acknowledging his bad intention) declared the same to a certain person of good
credit, whose name we here conceal for that he lives amongst the enemies. And
to say nothing whether this ought to be esteemed for a miracle or no, yet is it
worthy the consideration, to see God his evident providence in this matter.

How a lame woman was cured.
CAtharin Mos^ier wife of John Bailly dwelling in the town of A^h in the In
Dec. 1^0^
country of Henaul^, being in chyldbed, was taken with a certain disease
which caused in her the palsy, and stretching of her sin^wes on her left side,
whereby she became altogether lame, and when she walked it was with great
pain.

Whereupon her husband resolved to go in pilgrimage for her to our Lady at
Mo^ta^gu, to obtain there of our lady his wives health. The Same voyage
being made and his devotion ended, the said woman was perfectly cured of her
halting and lamenes, as it appears by the attestation of the Magistrates of
thesayd town of A^^ dated upon the last of December 1603. signed I. le
Merchier, and sealed with the seal of the same town.

How a possessed person was delu^^red by wood of the Oak of our Laedie.
CAthari^ de Bus daughter of the late In ^^^. 1604.
John de Bus dwelling in the City of Li^le in the Cou^tie of Fla^ters, in the
year 1602. being sixtee^ years of age or therabout was found to have been
possessed of the devil, who by diverse sleightes tru^peries and promises had
deceived and cir^umue^ted her: insomuch that she could be scarce a quarter of
an hour in peace, without being seized upon vexed and troubled by the enemy:
which made her speak (to the purpos) diverse sorts of languages, as Hebrew,
Greek and Latin: as master Michiel le Ca^del Pastor of the Parish of S.
Savior in the City of Lille, and Master Siluester Deuis priest of the same
Church solemnly avouched, as having heard and exorcized the said patient. Who
besides the speaking of these strange languages, did in fury things above all
natural and human force: so that it was necessary to have five or six men
to hold her: who notwithstanding were much troubled to keep and hold her down.
For when they came near unto her with the Blessed Sacrament of the altar she
wrythed and wrested herself strangely, both with her legs, arms, and back,
as with her neck and head, with a terrible countenance, gnashing of her teeth,
and grisely drawing of her mouth. The parents and friends of this wench labored
so much that she was diverse times exorcized, sometimes by certain fathers of
the order of the Capuchins, sometimes by other Priests, unto whom the wicked
spirits answered in diverse languages, confessing at that time that they were
seven in number, they spoke diverse injurious and scandalous things, and told
the faults of diverse that were present. So that one day while this Catharin
was exorcized in a Chapel of our Lady built in the honor of the hows of our
Lady of Lor^tto (which wa^ after the ^east of All Saints in the year 1603)
there was a report in the City of Lille that the town of Ostend (which as
then was kept by the rebels of Holland, and assieged by the army of our
Princes) was surrendered: the enemy was so bold as to say by the mouth of the
wench that it was not true, and that they should see so much ereit were long,
and that those that had bruted it abroad were certain thieves that came from
robbing the Cibo^re of the Blessed Sacrament in the town of Newport the which
they had as yet in their bag, and that the great master A (...) for church
robbers.
compelled them to say so much to accuse their sin. Which was afterward
found true. For upon the self same day two soldiers Suissers were cast into
prison in the said City of Lille, who had blazed abroad the report of the
aforesaid rendering of Ostend and the said Cibo^r was found amongst them, the
which they had stolen out of Newport, whether afterward they were carried, and
there put to death by order of Justice The priests continuing the said
exorcisines, after some four months the patient was delivered of one of those
wicked spirits, and after a while successively again of other three, giving
four evident signs of their departure, by breaking or cracking diverse pa^es
of the glass windo^s as otherwise. Having first and before they departed
thrown out at the mouth of the patient sometimes brimstone, sometimes pinnes
in great number, a bowed piece of silver of five sous, and a great nail of the
length of ones hand. After that again thesayd exorcisines were continued by
thesayd Sir Siluester Denis, both by the entreaty of the wenches parents, as
also by the commandment of the Lord Bishop of Tournay, and in the space of
two months by the ordinary exorcismes of the Catholic Church two other of the
enemies were cast out: and a month or five weeks after, again on other* And
although now seven wicked feendes (according to the number which they
themselves had discovered) were departed, yet the said Sir Siluester perceived
that the enemy had lied, and that the said wench was not yet cured. Wherefore
he ceased not to continue the exorcismes until the beginning of the year 1604,
within the octaues of the Epiphan^^ of our lord: when on a time the said Sir
Siluester exorcising the patient in the presence of a great multitude of
people: the devil began to cry out; and speak to one that was there present
these words. Art thou there also? I know well enough from whence thou come;
and what thou have brought with thee: thou art one of them that has been
visiting Ma^te of Montaigu. It was true that the parents and friends of the said
wench had made a vow to go in Pilgrimage to our Lady at Montaigu to pray
there for her cure. At these words the people began to look about them, who he
should be of whom the enemy had spoken, and there was found a man that was
come from Montaigu, and had brought with him a piece of the Oak of our Lady.
Whereupon Sir Siluester took the said piece; and made the patient to eat it,
and immediately after she had swallowed it, the enemy (who called himself
Ho^illi^, Ch^que^, and Clinq^art) showed himself in her throat, crying out that
he scorched and burned, because of the wood which was eaten: and he added* that
he was compelled to depart, and that there remained in her as yet three: and
being deman^ded by the exorcist by whose merit and intercession he was to
depart? The wicked fee^d answered; of Mar^^ of Montaigu. And afterward being
demanded what sign he would give of his departure? He said: he would burst a
glass of the Church window. And immediately after, two of the^ departed with
the said sign of bursting the glass, and the third saying that he was the
last of ten, cried out (in going forth) with a loud voice. V^^e N. Dame de
Montaigu, qui nous faict sortir. Honor be to our Lady of Montaigu, who makes
us to depart. He being compelled to speak these words (as with reason we may
presume) by M^^. 1. M^^^. 3. Luc 4. (...). ^^.
the majesty and sovereign power of God; even as we have in the Gospel, that
the devils in their departing gave testimony that our Lord Jesus Christ was
the son of God. And in going he plucked out a great nail that was fastened
deep in the wall, the which he threw against the window, but yet touched it not.

And from that day afterward the said Catharin remained whole and perfectly
free from the possession and vexation of the enemy: inioying all her limbs
and senses as freely as ever she did before. And about the beginning of May the
said Catharin accompained with the said Sir Siluester Denis and Peter du ^rieu
her uncle went toward Montaigu, where she remained for nine days, going to
confession and communion and daily visiting the Chapel of our Lady, yielding
tha^cks to God, and to his holy Mother for the mercy which she had received.
And all this that has here been said is manifest both by the deposition and
attestation of the said Catharin, of the said Sir Siluester and Peter du Trieu
made under their oaths before the Pastor of Sichen, Master Anthony de
Bouckhout Maier, and Sir Bartholmew Thichon Chaplain of our Ladies: as also by
an other attestation made and passed under the oaths of the said persons, and
with them of Sir Michel le Candel, and Marie du Bus wife of the aforesaid
Peter, before the Magistrates of the City of Lille, upon the first of June, in
the said year 1604. according to a writing composed hereof, dated as above,
sealed with the great seal of the said City and signed P. Mout^n.

How a Child that was burst was afterward cured.
GErard van Omel wyk-maister of the In May 1604.
City of Antwerp, and Susan VVagemaker, hi^ wife, had in the year 1903. a

Whereupon some dissuaded her to go any further as she did not, but stayed at

she did hear deuoutely, praying for her chyldes health. This done she

taking from the chylds body his trusse, she found him perfectly healed:
insomuch that she never needed to bynd him therewith afterward, for so much
(I say) as the child remained in perfect health, as being intierly cured. As
this Gerard and his wife testified and declared under their solemn oaths,
